$fesken/vi-m_FESK+IN $/vi-m_+IN\n
{="swaddle?". Millett (1982) following Colborn (1940) suggests a miswriting in the\n
common exemplar of S for R and emends to FERKIN < OE fercian. This usually\n
means "convey, bring" but is attested in OE with the meanings "support,\n
feed". I think it unlikely, however, that the scribes of B and T would\n
both have perpetuated such a mistake. I favour MED\'s reading, which\n
invokes Latin fasciare and OF faissier "swaddle". Godefroy lists among\n
the many attested forms for the related noun faisse, the variant\n
fesche. A form *fescher could be Anglicised as FESKIN in early Middle\n
English, cf. "task" < OF tasche=}\n
